  278. Just comb it into your face fur and enjoy. It doesn't get any easier than that. The smell was strange the first time I used it, but just suck it up and enjoy your new awesomeness.<br /><br />Update: I have found it best to slip the teeth of my comb over the rim of the can and scrape out a little bit of Balm, then combing it into the hairs. You will waste less balm and the balm still in the can stays neat and flat. I first tried to scrape some out with a fingertip and wipe it on, but that didn't work at all. It may work for short beards.<br /><br />My beard is fairly long at about 4 inches, so I usually dip the comb twice but be careful not to use too much Balm or your beard will be shiny and have a greasy feel to it. However, I happen to like how it makes my hands feel so I always over-apply. Your experience may vary. A little bit will go a long way, it just takes more comb strokes to evenly apply small amounts. It will coat your comb like paint coats a brush, so if you want a thin coat, brush more than you dip.<br /><br />I happen to work outdoors all day so it makes more sense for me to apply Beard Balm after work. Otherwise all sorts of wildlife and pollen will stick to it. After work I comb in the Balm and all of the tangles and wild hairs are very easily tamed with the bare minimum of pulled hairs. The detritus in your now-glowing beard will mostly be sticking to your comb rather than your face. Wash your hands with some soap and use some of the lather to clean the oils from the comb. Voila! You now have an awesome looking beard and a clean comb, soft hands and a spring in your step.

  449. I've never used any sort of beard products before, so I have nothing to compare this product to, but after a couple months of using it I am satisfied. After seeing a lot of the silly reviews about lumberjacks and manliness I was sceptical that any of them were genuine. Their product website is pretty much the same way, which leads me to believe that many of the reviews were left by the manufacturers. Positives: It really makes my beard softer, and gives it a bit of a glow. A little goes a long way, I've had it for almost 2 months now and still have about half a can left after daily use. If it's not used for a few days in a row, beard is noticeably dryer and more tangled. This stuff makes a big difference for sure. Negatives: The smell. Some reviews say it goes away after 20 minutes or so, which isn't true. Your nose just gets used to it so you don't notice it after some time, but run your fingers through your beard and you'll see that it is infact still there. It's not a bad smell per say, just unnecessary. And no, the majority of women, even those who like beards, don't like the smell. There aren't any instructions, the can comes all by itself. Granted, it's not something you can screw up, but for a first time user some pointers would be helpful. Their website has an instructions page, but it's pretty much a joke about put it on any time you want to feel like a man. It's a good product that I would likely buy again, but I will also try others to compare it with. My advice if you do buy it, is to use a little after a shower while your beard is still wet. It's easier to apply that way, and you use less of the product. Using it on a dry beard makes your beard a bit sticky and clumpy, whereas application to a damp beard yields much better results. Don't brush your beard after using it, because you'll never get it, or its smell, off your brush. Then the brush gets sticky and starts collecting crap that then gets transferred to your beard the next time you useit.

  585. Have you ever wondered how you can smell more like your mechanic? If so, this beard balm is the answer!<br /><br />Disclaimer: I bought this product to do market research, as I am a producer and seller of beard products, including balms. I am not trolling this product, just giving an insider's point of view from someone who has tried all the balms, oils, and waxes available on the market and providing some insight into how their recipe compares to others. I am not going to be a jerk and say the name of my brand because it isn't kosher to steal sales that way.<br /><br />The ingredients are nothing special compared to anything else on the market, so really you have to base it on smell. While smell is totally subjective, I can tell you that this captures the exact smell of my grandfather after a day of working on his industrial machinery out in his shop. It's not necessarily bad, but it's necessarily great either. On the plus side, it smells like an honest days' work, which is sort of satisfying and manly, but not how I want to smell all the time. Apart from my sensibilities, when I showed this to potential customers during market research it was never selected as the favorite. So, if you want your beard to be sniffed and scruffed by potential lovers, this may not be the perfect balm for you.<br /><br />To my nose, the overwhelming scent here is geranium oil and the lanolin, which is a fatty oil that's a byproduct of the wool industry. I can't pick up the lemon at all, and the eucalyptus is quite faint. Lanolin is actually very beneficial for the skin, but carries with it a mild sheepy smell. It is slightly strange that Beard Balm decided to go with Lanolin instead of the more commonly used shea butter. I would rate this balm 2 stars based on smell, but using lanolin as the base is a more gutsy choice than others and this balm might provide additional benefits if used with a shea butter based balm in rotation--I bumped it up to 3 stars. Variety is the spice of life, as they say. Long story short: if you have an allergy or aversion to lanolin or sheep's wool, this product is not for you!<br /><br />The oil seems to be light-bodied and I'm guessing that lanolin makes up about 75% of the overall mix, possibly more. I can't detect any beeswax smell and it doesn't give my beard that characteristic &#34;crunch&#34; hold that comes with beeswax. If I had to guess, I'd say they have about 15% beeswax in the mix, possibly less. The remaining composition seems to come from coconut oil, but there is no coconut smell to be found, which is sort of a shame to my nose. I could be wrong here and they could be using refined coconut oil, but it's hard to know.<br /><br />As far as balms go, this one is slighty above average and I feel like the ingredients themselves are high-quality. If this is your first foray into beard balms, I would recommend trying another brand first, if only because the scent is unquestionably divisive. I'd actually recommend that you only use a balm if your beard is quite young (say, less than 6 weeks) since the main benefit to a balm is that it conditions the face and reduces the terrible itchy beard phase. If your beard is of a more substantial length, stick with oils which are more readily absorbed and beneficial to your hair. You can break out the balm if you want a change, or if you find that it has enough styling hold for you.
